Kingdom","ticket_url":null,"ticket_type":null,"ticket_status":"unavailable","on_sale_datetime":null,"facebook_rsvp_url":"http://www.bandsintown.com/event/10701122?app_id=ONTOUR_1638&artist=The+Staves&came_from=67","description":"The Staves\nwith support from James Canty.\n\nThe Platform (Lincoln Students' Union)\nThursday 29th October, Doors 7pm\nTickets from www.engineshed.co.uk\n\nJust one listen to Blood I Bled EP will tell you The Staves have changed since their debut album was released in 2012. Of course, the sisters haven't abandoned their beautiful, signature close harmonies, but they have bolstered them with a clutch of multi-layered, hugely ambi-tious songs, recorded with the scale and confidence that can only come after three years on the road.\n\nThe aforementioned Blood I Bled opens The Staves' forthcoming second album If I Was, and was indeed the first track written, recorded, and released from the album, hinting at the world of possibilities Emily, Jessica and Camilla have gone on to explore.\n\n\"It almost made it onto the first album,\" says Camilla, \"but it just wasn't ready. It didn't sit with anything else and we didn't really know how to finish it off.\"\n\nThe song lay dormant while they performed all over the world, including appearing alongside Mumford & Sons during their Glastonbury headlining slot in 2013 and several tours with American cult heroes Bon Iver. Having formed strong friendships with the latter band's found-er Justin Vernon and his assembled gaggle of players, the sisters were invited to his April Base studio in Wisconsin to work on whatever music they had in a relaxed, idyllic setting.\n\n\"There was no plan to make a record there, or even demo anything, it was initially just to hang out and play some music with Justin. There was no pressure at all, we didn't even tell our label we were going.\"\n\nPretty soon Blood I Bled, along with a handful of other song ideas had been resurrected, re-written and roughly recorded, with one trip to Wisconsin quickly leading to another, when things were made more official.\n\n\"We demoed about 10 songs and then asked ourselves 'Arent we actually just making a record?'\" says Emily, adding Vernon seemed equally unsure whether he was in fact producing The Staves' second album or not.\n\n\"It was a bit like when you first start seeing someone and you have to define the relationship,\" says Jessica. \"You have to work out what you're calling it and if you're telling your friends about it.\"\n\nFortunately for all, The Staves and Vernon did become a metaphorical couple, and they got to work more seriously. The resulting album, made during The Staves' five eventual visits to Wisconsin, is as stunning as the snow-covered landscape it was recorded in; at once deeply personal to each sister, fuelled by heartbreak and individual turbulence, it's also full of hope, redemption and positivity for an uncertain future.\n\nThe album was born, in some ways, out of intense frustration. While three years on the road is a privilege not to be sniffed at, it did mean the trio were unable to work on any new ideas they'd had in any detail.\n\n\"We hadn't created anything in so long,\" says Camilla. \"We were really itching to have a break and to let out all this stuff that we hadn't had chance to express. Fortunately we found a place with Justin's studio where we were allowed to do whatever wanted. It was the most lib-erating experience, being able to record until 4 in the morning, or while drunk. Whatever worked  there was no idea too silly. It was like a school trip with no parents.\"\n\n\"It was magical,\" adds Jessica. \"The snow was neck-high outside, so we were sort of trapped inside. Cabin fever sets in, but its really conducive to working.\n\n\"We quickly realised there was a lot in each of us that we needed to write aboutso many things had happened.\"\n\n\"The amount of time we've spent away from home has affected all our relationships,\" contin-ues Emily. \"And I don't just mean boyfriends, but relationships with family and close friends and wider groups of mates, who you just have to get used to never seeing. It can be difficult. Writing about it all is necessary therapy in making sense of quite an unconventional life.\"\n\nAvoiding the dreaded pitfall of writing a second album about touring, The Staves have clever-ly opted to address the issue from another perspective, examining what they've left behind rather than endless motorways, hotel rooms and what they see in front of them.\n\nOnce in Wisconsin and buoyed by the trusting working environment, the ideas started flowing freely. All three praise Vernon's ability to leave them in charge of the recordings while facilitat-ing their ideas, bringing to life arrangements and orchestration they'd written but weren't sure how to realise.\n\nCases in point are Black And White and Teeth White, which show yet another side to The Staves this second time around. Both songs see Jessica putting down her acoustic guitar and plugging in an electric, and with Black And White in particular, find the sisters singing attack-ing, abrasive backing vocals in a way they've never done before.\n\nKeen to avoid these two electric songs sounding like contrived dalliances in a different genre, the arrangements are much more intelligent and subtle than merely dialing in some distortion and turning up the drums. Indeed, it's that tension between expanse and restraint, furthering their sound while maintaining the familiar, which makes If I Was such an enthralling album to listen to.\n\nBlood I Bled, for example, builds and builds until its denouement shifts the song from minor to major and has the effect of the sun burning through the clouds after a storm. Or, in The Staves' words, \"like the moment Elliott's bike takes off at the end of E.T.\"\n\nOn a similarly filmic note, The Shining, meanwhile  so called because the Jack Nicholson classic was playing in the control room while Emily was writing the lyrics  fades in and out, as if drifting into an existing conversation and leaving before it's over.\n\nSteady was the seamless joining together of two songs written by Jessica and Camilla, while Horizons is among the most optimistic songs on the album, dealing with leaving baggage be-hind and moving forward. It was written simultaneously by all three Staves, each going off to a different corner of the studio to write their respective parts. We were expecting an incoher-ent mess, but strangely what we each had written independently came together without any discussion. I guess thats when we realized just how in tune we can be, says Jessica.\n\nThe closing 1-2 of Make It Holy (recorded on the guitar Vernon used on breakout hit Skinny Love), and Sadness Don't Own Me, is as fitting an end to If I Was as is possible to imagine. Reflecting on the past, the songs are at first filled with sadness and contemplation before evolving to defiance and hope, with The Staves' voices proving, yet again, that no matter how they're
